  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>This issue only appears to happen in Network Server/Client mode. Embedded mode does not have the issue.</p> 
                  <p>My timezone is American/Chicago. Saving timestamps with values for the 6 hours prior to DST start are being read back in as values 1 hour later than written. (I believe the issue happens on the write because values written in Network Server/Client mode and read in Embedded mode are incorrect, while values written and read in Embedded mode are corect.)</p> 
                  <p>Values between 3/13/2010 - 20:00 CST and 3/14/2010 - 02:00 CST will return timstamps 1 hour off. The "setTimestamp" method is being passed a GMT calendar with the timestamp:</p> 
                  <p>I have a complete test class I can attach, but here is a summary:</p> 
                  <p>private final TimeZone gmtTZ = TimeZone.getTimeZone("GMT");<br> private final Calendar gmtCal = Calendar.getInstance(gmtTZ);<br> ...<br> String sql = "INSERT INTO app.dst_test (id, gmt_timestamp, milli_time) VALUES(?,?,?)";<br> String sql2 = "SELECT * from app.dst_test where id=?";<br> ...<br> ps.setTimestamp(2, ts, gmtCal);<br> ...<br> Timestamp tsRead = rs.getTimestamp("gmt_timestamp", gmtCal);<br> ...</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

\u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12854866_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'08\\/Apr\\/10 08:36\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-08T08:36:41+0000\'\u003e08\\/Apr\\/10 08:36\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI think I see what\'s going on now. The setTimestamp() method in the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nclient driver, and its siblings setTime() and setDate(), use the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nsupplied Calendar object to determine which timezone to convert the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ntimestamp to before storing it. The way it does this, is by adjusting\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe timestamp by the same amount of time as the timezone difference\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nbetween the supplied calendar and the default calendar.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAlthough this adjustment will give the desired effect most of the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ntime, it is broken because it actually changes the timestamp to point\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nto a different point in time. Therefore it will miss on the exact time\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nof the DST changes with a couple of hours and we see these\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndiscrepancies. We should only use the calendar to change the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npresentation of timestamp, not to change its value.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI did the following experiment with the client code:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e  1) removed the code that adjusts the timestamp value\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e  2) passed the calendar object down to the code that writes the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n     timestamp to the network stream\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e  3) used the calendar object to extract the timezone-adjusted date\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n     and time out of the timezone\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSince in (3) we now have the unmodified timestamp value, there\'s no\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nskew that confuses the conversion to the requested timezone, not even\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\naround time of the DST change.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo with these changes, the correct values were sent from the client to\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe server. However, there was still one discrepancy between the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nvalues sent from the client and what\'s actually stored (this is an\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nimprovement, though, since there were six discrepancies without the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nchange).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis last discrepancy was caused by the handling of the timestamp on\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe server. The server does not use any Calendar object explicitly\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nwhen parsing what it gets from the client or when storing the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ntimestamp in the database. The default timezone will therefore be used\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nin the handling of the timestamp. So when the client sends the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ntimestamp 2010-03-14 02:01:00, which is a perfectly fine timestamp in\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe GMT timezone and many other timezones, the server (or more\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nprecisely, Timestamp.valueOf(String)) thinks the timestamp refers to a\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\npoint in time within the \\\"lost\\\" hour in the America\\/Chicago timezone,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nand it silently adjusts it to 03:01:00 so that it\'s valid in that\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ntimezone too.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSince we don\'t store the timezone together with the timestamp, it\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndoesn\'t matter much which timezone the server uses when handling it,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nas long as it\'s consistent. However, since timezones that observe DST\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nlose one hour when switching to DST, calendars using that timezone\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ncannot reliably be used to represent times in other timezones. If the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nserver instead had used a timezone that doesn\'t observe DST, like GMT,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe timestamp wouldn\'t change on its way from the wire to the database\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\neven if the timestamp on the wire is not a valid time in the local\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ntimezone.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWith this in mind, I extended my experiment with the following changes\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nin the server code (DRDAConnThread):\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e  4) when reading the (timezone-less) timestamp string sent from the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n     client, put the values into a Calendar object with timezone set\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n     to GMT, and generate the timestamp from that Calendar\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e  5) use setTimestamp(int,Timestamp,Calendar) instead of\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n     setTimestamp(int,Timestamp) when passing the value to the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n     embedded driver, with the Calendar\'s timezone set to GMT\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis took care of the last discrepancy and made the client\\/server\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nsetup store the exact same values on disk as the embedded setup did.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, there\'s still one error when reading the values back to the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nclient, as noted in a previous comment about the incorrect reading of\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthe values generated by the embedded test. I haven\'t investigated this\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nproblem yet, but I assume it\'s similar to the problems described\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nabove.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"knutanders\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12854866_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=knutanders\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12854866_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'08\\/Apr\\/10 08:36\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-08T08:36:41+0000\'\u003e08\\/Apr\\/10 08:36\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I think I see what\'s going on now. The setTimestamp() method in the \\nclient driver, and its siblings setTime() and setDate(), use the \\nsupplied Calendar object to determine which timezone to convert the \\ntimestamp to before storing it. The way it does this, is by adjusting \\nthe timestamp by the same amount of time as the timezone difference \\nbetween the supplied calendar and the default calendar. \\n\\n Although this adjustment will give the desired effect most of the \\ntime, it is broken because it actually changes the timestamp to point \\nto a different point in time. Therefore it will miss on the exact time \\nof the DST changes with a couple of hours and we see these \\ndiscrepancies. We should only use the calendar to change the \\npresentation of timestamp, not to change its value. \\n\\n I did the following experiment with the client code: \\n\\n   1) removed the code that adjusts the timestamp value \\n\\n   2) passed the calendar object down to the code that writes the \\n     timestamp to the network stream \\n\\n   3) used the calendar object to extract the timezone-adjusted date \\n     and time out of the timezone \\n\\n Since in (3) we now have the unmodified timestamp value, there\'s no \\nskew that confuses the conversion to the requested timezone, not even \\naround time of the DST change. \\n\\n So with these changes, the correct values were sent from the client to \\nthe server. However, there was still one discrepancy between the \\nvalues sent from the client and what\'s actually stored (this is an \\nimprovement, though, since there were six discrepancies without the \\nchange). \\n\\n This last discrepancy was caused by the handling of the timestamp on \\nthe server. The server does not use any Calendar object explicitly \\nwhen parsing what it gets from the client or when storing the \\ntimestamp in the database. The default timezone will therefore be used \\nin the handling of the timestamp. So when the client sends the \\ntimestamp 2010-03-14 02:01:00, which is a perfectly fine timestamp in \\nthe GMT timezone and many other timezones, the server (or more \\nprecisely, Timestamp.valueOf(String)) thinks the timestamp refers to a \\npoint in time within the \\\"lost\\\" hour in the America\\/Chicago timezone, \\nand it silently adjusts it to 03:01:00 so that it\'s valid in that \\ntimezone too. \\n\\n Since we don\'t store the timezone together with the timestamp, it \\ndoesn\'t matter much which timezone the server uses when handling it, \\nas long as it\'s consistent. However, since timezones that observe DST \\nlose one hour when switching to DST, calendars using that timezone \\ncannot reliably be used to represent times in other timezones. If the \\nserver instead had used a timezone that doesn\'t observe DST, like GMT, \\nthe timestamp wouldn\'t change on its way from the wire to the database \\neven if the timestamp on the wire is not a valid time in the local \\ntimezone. \\n\\n With this in mind, I extended my experiment with the following changes \\nin the server code (DRDAConnThread): \\n\\n   4) when reading the (timezone-less) timestamp string sent from the \\n     client, put the values into a Calendar object with timezone set \\n     to GMT, and generate the timestamp from that Calendar \\n\\n   5) use setTimestamp(int,Timestamp,Calendar) instead of \\n     setTimestamp(int,Timestamp) when passing the value to the \\n     embedded driver, with the Calendar\'s timezone set to GMT \\n\\n This took care of the last discrepancy and made the client\\/server \\nsetup store the exact same values on disk as the embedded setup did. \\n\\n However, there\'s still one error when reading the values back to the \\nclient, as noted in a previous comment about the incorrect reading of \\nthe values generated by the embedded test. I haven\'t investigated this \\nproblem yet, but I assume it\'s similar to the problems described \\nabove.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n on the fix for this issue. It looks to me as if there are four bugs in the timestamp handling (and some of these also apply to date and time) that need to be solved:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e1) The time skew issue that makes the client miss on the exact time of the DST switch when converting from local tz to GMT\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e2) Timestamps that are not valid in the local timezone are silently changed when the server reads them from the client\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e3) Timestamps that are not valid in the local timezone are silently changed when the server reads them from the database\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e4) Timestamps that are not valid in the local timezone are silently changed when the client reads them from the server\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFixing (1) will make the number of discrepancies in the original repro go down from six to one. It looks to me as if there are four bugs in the timestamp handling (and some of these also apply to date and time) that need to be solved: \\n\\n 1) The time skew issue that makes the client miss on the exact time of the DST switch when converting from local tz to GMT \\n\\n 2) Timestamps that are not valid in the local timezone are silently changed when the server reads them from the client \\n\\n 3) Timestamps that are not valid in the local timezone are silently changed when the server reads them from the database \\n\\n 4) Timestamps that are not valid in the local timezone are silently changed when the client reads them from the server \\n\\n Fixing (1) will make the number of discrepancies in the original repro go down from six to one. \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eThe attached patch derby-4582-3a-server-send.diff modifies DRDAConnThread to address issue (3). It makes the server use a GMT calendar when reading TIME, DATE or TIMESTAMP values out of the database, and uses the same GMT calendar to format the string representation that it sends to the client. This way, the value read from the database is not silently changed if it happens to represent a time that is not valid in the local time zone.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWith this patch, the values are sent correctly from the client, stored correctly in the database and sent correctly back to the client. It makes the server use a GMT calendar when reading TIME, DATE or TIMESTAMP values out of the database, and uses the same GMT calendar to format the string representation that it sends to the client. I noticed that DaylightSavingTest failed if I changed it to insert the values into VARCHAR columns instead of TIMESTAMP, TIME and DATE. The problem was with the method in CrossConverters that parses the date portion of a DATE or a TIMESTAMP when converting from a VARCHAR value. It didn\'t take into account that java.util.Calendar counts months from 0.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe attached patch adds test cases that test conversion between VARCHAR and date\\/time values in DaylightSavingTest, and fixes the off-by-one-month bug.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eRunning the rest of the regression tests now.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"knutanders\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12861478_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=knutanders\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12861478_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'27\\/Apr\\/10 18:07\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2010-04-27T18:07:28+0000\'\u003e27\\/Apr\\/10 18:07\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Some of the code added in the 4a patch wasn\'t exercised by any of the existing tests, so of course it contained a bug.
